§ 10.01 HOW CODE DESIGNATED AND CITED.
   The ordinances contained in this title and the following titles, chapters
and sections shall constitute and be designated the “Code of the City of
Kingwood, West Virginia”, and may be so cited. Such ordinances may also be
cited as the “Kingwood City Code”, “city code” or “code of ordinances”.
(1991 Code, § 1-1)
Statutory reference:
   Authority of City Council to adopt a comprehensive code of ordinances, see
W. Va. Code § 8-11-4(b)
§ 10.02 DEFINITIONS AND RULES OF CONSTRUCTION.
   In the construction of this code and of all other ordinances and resolutions
of the City Council, the following definitions and rules of construction shall
be observed, unless it shall be expressly provided otherwise by any section,
ordinance or resolution, unless inconsistent with the manifest intent of the
City Council or unless the context clearly requires otherwise.
   AUTHORITY OF OFFICERS. Whenever authority is conferred on or an act is
required to be performed by a city officer, such authority may be exercised or
performed, at the instance of such officer, by a deputy, agent or subordinate,
unless such authority cannot lawfully be deputed.
   CITY. The City of Kingwood, West Virginia.
   CITY CODE; THIS CODE. The Code of the City of Kingwood, West Virginia, as
amended and currently in effect.
    CITY COUNCIL; THE COUNCIL. The Council of the City of Kingwood, West
Virginia.
   COMPUTATION OF TIME; REASONABLE TIME. The time within which an act is to be
done shall be computed by excluding the first day and including the last; or,
if the last day be Sunday or a holiday, it shall also be excluded; but this
provision shall not be deemed to change any rule of law applicable to bills of
exchange or negotiable instruments; provided, that if time is expressed in
hours, the whole of any Sunday or holiday shall be excluded, unless the clear
intent of the Council is to the contrary. In all cases where provision is made
for an act to be done or notice to be given within a REASONABLE TIME, it shall
be construed to mean only such time as may be necessary, under the
circumstances then and there existing, for the prompt performance of such act
or the giving of such notice.
   COUNTY. The County of Preston, West Virginia.
   GENDER. A word importing the masculine gender only may be construed to
include the feminine and neuter as well as the masculine.
   GENERAL RULE. All general provisions, terms, phrases and expressions shall
be liberally construed in order that the true intent and meaning of the City
Council may be fully carried out. Words and phrases shall be taken in their
usual sense, but technical words having a peculiar and appropriate meaning in
law shall be understood according to their technical import.
   JOINT AUTHORITY. All words giving a JOINT AUTHORITY to three or more persons
or officers shall be construed as giving such JOINT AUTHORITY to a majority of
such persons or officers, and not to any lesser number.
   MONTH and YEAR. The word MONTH shall mean a calendar month; the word YEAR
shall mean a calendar year; the word YEAR alone shall be equivalent to the
expression YEAR OF OUR LORD.
   MUNICIPALITY. The City of Kingwood, West Virginia.
   NUMBER. A word importing the singular number only may be applied to several
persons or things, as well as to one person or thing; a word importing the
plural number only may be applied to one person or thing as well as to several.
   OATH; SWORN. A solemn affirmation shall be the equivalent to an oath in all
cases, unless otherwise expressly provided, and the word OATH shall be deemed
to include an affirmation and the word SWEAR or SWORN to be complied with if
the person referred to makes solemn affirmation.
   OFFICERS, DEPARTMENTS AND THE LIKE. Officers, departments, boards,
commissions and employees referred to in this code shall mean officers,
departments, boards, commissions and employees of the City of Kingwood, unless
the content clearly indicates otherwise.
   OWNER. As applied to any property, any part owner, joint owner, tenant in
common, tenant in partnership, joint tenant or tenant by the entirety of the
whole or of a part of such property.
   PERSON. A corporation, firm, partnership, association, society, club or any
other group acting as a unit, as well as an individual, unless restricted
within the context.
   PERSONAL PROPERTY. Goods, chattels, real and personal, money, credits,
investments and the evidence thereof.
   PRECEDING; FOLLOWING. Next before and next after, respectively.
   PREMISES. When used as applicable to real property, shall include land and
buildings.
   PROPERTY. Real, personal and mixed property.
   REAL PROPERTY; REAL ESTATE; LAND; LANDS. Lands, buildings, tenements and
hereditaments and all rights thereto and interests therein, except chattel
interests.
   SHALL; MAY. The word SHALL is mandatory; the word MAY is permissive.
   SIDEWALK. The portion of a street between the curb line or, where there is
no curb, the lateral lines of a roadway and the adjacent property line,
intended for the use of pedestrians. If there is no public area between the
lateral lines of the roadway and the abutting property line, then that area
immediately abutting the street line shall be considered SIDEWALK AREA.
   SIGNATURE or SUBSCRIPTION BY MARK. A mark made by a signer or subscriber who
cannot write, such signer’s or subscriber’s name being written near the mark by
a witness who shall write his or her own name near the signer’s or subscriber’s
name.
   STATE. The State of West Virginia.
   STATE CODE REFERENCES. References to the West Virginia Code shall be to the
Official Code of West Virginia, 1931, as amended and currently in effect.
   STREET. Alley, avenue, boulevard, highway, road, lane, viaduct, bridge and
approaches thereto, and all other public thoroughfares in the city, and the
entire width thereof between abutting property lines; also a sidewalk or
footpath, unless the contrary is expressed or unless such construction would be
inconsistent with the intent of the City Council.
   TENANT or OCCUPANT. Applied to a building or land, any person holding a
written or oral lease to or who occupies the whole or part of such building or
land, either alone or with others.
    TENSES. The present tense includes the past and future tenses; the future
includes the present.
   WRITING. Includes any form of recorded message comprehensible by ordinary
visual means. Whenever any notice, report, statement or record is required or
authorized by this code or other ordinance or resolution of the city, it shall
be made in writing in the English language, unless it is expressly provided
otherwise.
Statutory reference:
   Acts by agent or deputy, see W. Va. Code § 2-2-5
   Computation of time, see W. Va. Code § 2-2-3
   Construction of statutes, see W. Va. Code §§ 2-2-10, 2-2-10(a), 2-2-10(b),
2-2-10(d)
   Corresponding state law relating to construction of statutes, see W. Va.
Code § 2-2-10(c)
   Definition of “personal property” relating to construction of statutes, see
W. Va. Code § 2-2-10(q)
   Definition of “property” relating to the construction of statutes, see W.
Va. Code § 2-2-10(r)
   Definition of “real property” relating to the construction of statutes, see
W. Va. Code § 2-2-10(p)
   Definition of “writing” relating to the construction of statutes, see W. Va.
Code § 2-2-10(c)
   Definitions of “person” relating to the construction of statutes, see W. Va.
Code § 2-2-10(I)
   Definitions of words and phrases in the Municipal Code of West Virginia, see
W. Va. Code §§ 8-1-1, 8-1-2
   Month; year; fiscal year, see W. Va. Code § 2-2-4
   Oath; sworn, see W. Va. Code § 2-2-7
§ 10.03 PROVISIONS CONSIDERED AS CONTINUATIONS OF EXISTING ORDINANCES.
   The provisions appearing in this code, insofar as they are substantially the
same as those of ordinances in effect immediately preceding the effective date
of this code and included herein, shall be considered as continuations thereof
and not as new enactments.
§ 10.04 CATCHLINES AND HEADINGS OF PORTIONS OF CODE.
   The chapter, subchapter, division and section headings of this code are
intended as mere catchwords to indicate the contents thereof and shall not be
deemed or taken to be titles thereof, nor as any part thereof; nor, unless
expressly so provided, shall they be so deemed when any of such chapters,
subchapters, divisions or sections, including the headings or catchlines, are
amended or reenacted.
Statutory reference:
   Construction of statutes, see W. Va. Code §§ 2-2-10(z), 2-2-12
§ 10.05 SEVERABILITY OF PARTS OF THIS CODE, AND OF CODES AND OTHER REGULATIONS
ADOPTED BY REFERENCE.
   It is hereby declared to be the intention of the City Council that the
sections, divisions, paragraphs, sentences, clauses and phrases of this code
and of each of the technical codes and other regulations herein adopted by
reference are severable, and that if any phrase, clause, sentence, paragraph,
division or section of this code or of any such technical code or other
regulations shall be declared unconstitutional or invalid by the valid judgment
or decree of any court of competent jurisdiction, such unconstitutionality or
invalidity shall not affect any of the remaining phrases, clauses, sentences,
paragraphs, divisions and sections thereof, since they would have been enacted
by the City Council without the incorporation therein of any such
unconstitutional or invalid phrase, clause, sentence, paragraph, division or
section.
§ 10.06 EFFECT OF REPEAL OR EXPIRATION OF ORDINANCE.
   (A)   The repeal of an ordinance or its expiration, by virtue of any
provision contained therein, shall not affect any right accrued, any offense
committed, any penalty or punishment incurred or any proceeding commenced
before the repeal took effect or the ordinance expired.
    (B)   When any ordinance which repealed another shall itself be repealed,
the previous ordinance shall not be revived without express words to that
effect.
Statutory reference:
   Effect of repeal or expiration of statutes, see W. Va. Code § 2-2-8
   Repeal of an act repealing a statute, see W. Va. Code § 2-2-9
§ 10.99 PENALTY.
   Wherever in this code or in any ordinance or resolution of the City Council
or in any rule, regulation, notice or order promulgated by any officer or
agency of the city under authority duly vested in him, her or it, any act is
prohibited or is declared to be unlawful or an offense or a misdemeanor or the
doing of any act is required or the failure to do any act is declared to be
unlawful or an offense or a misdemeanor, and no specific penalty is provided
for the violation thereof, the violation of any such provision of this code or
of any such ordinance, resolution, rule, regulation, notice or order shall be
punished by a reasonable fine, not exceeding $500 or by imprisonment for a term
not to exceed 30 days or by both such fine and imprisonment. Each day any
violation of this code or of any such ordinance, resolution, rule, regulation,
notice or order shall constitute, except where otherwise provided, a separate
offense.
Statutory reference:
   State law as to penalties authorized to be imposed, subject to certain
limitations, for violations of municipal ordinances and means available to
municipalities for the recovery thereof, see W. Va. Code §§ 8-11-1, 8-12-5(55)

§ 30.01 SALARIES OF ELECTED OFFICIALS.
   (A)   The elected officials of the city shall receive a fixed salary or
compensation for services rendered as an elected official of the city, and said
fixed salary or compensation shall be applicable to the various elected
officials of the city as follows.
      (1)   The Mayor shall receive the amount of $3,500 per year, being paid
the amount of $116.67, less required payroll deductions, per regular or special
Council meeting that is attended by the Mayor for a maximum number of 30
meetings per year. Should the Mayor attend additional Council meeting in excess
of 30 meetings per year as held by the city, then the Mayor shall not be paid
any wages for the said additional Council meeting in excess of 30 per year.
      (2)   The Recorder shall receive a salary not to exceed the amount of
$2,500 per year, being paid the amount of $83.33, less required payroll
deductions, per regular or special Council meeting that is attended by the
Recorder for a maximum number of 30 meetings per year. Should the Recorder
attend additional Council meetings in excess of 30 meeting per year a held by
the city, then the Recorder shall not be paid any wages for the said additional
Council meetings in excess of 30 per year,
      (3)   Each of the Council members of the city shall receive a salary not
to exceed the amount of $1,500 per year, being paid the amount of $50, less
required payroll deductions, per regular or special Council meeting that is
attended by the Council member for a maximum number of 30 meetings per year as
held by the city, then the Council member shall not be paid any wages for the
said additional Council meetings in excess of 30 per year.
   (B)   For the purpose of this section, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
      COUNCIL MEETING. The regularly scheduled second and fourth Tuesday of
each month Council meeting and any and all special Council meetings as called
for by the City Council at which time the Council attends, a quorum is
established and at which meeting Council may vote on matters affecting the
City. COUNCIL MEETING does not include work meetings at which votes may not be
taken or any other special meeting which is not called as a regular or special
Council meeting.
      COUNCIL MEETING THAT IS ATTENDED BY. Such regularly or specially
scheduled Council meetings at which a quorum is established, Council may vote
on issues affecting the city and at which said meeting the Council member,
including the Mayor and Recorder, must be present at the time that quorum is
established or said Council member, including the Mayor and Recorder, shall not
be paid for attendance at said meeting. It is further provided that should any
member of Council, including the Mayor and Recorder, not be present at the time
that quorum is established, said member of Council, including the Mayor and
Recorder, shall not be paid for attendance at said meeting, regardless if said
member does appear and attend said Council meeting at some period of time
following the establishment of quorum.
      QUORUM IS ESTABLISHED. As being at such time as the first order of
business of the Council meeting is considered. Said first order of business
shall be in accordance with the agenda for each meeting as previously posted.
(Ord. 27, passed 3-24-2015; Ord. 27, passed 8-27-2019)
§ 30.02 POLICY.
   (A)   Statutory meeting location. All official meetings of the duly elected
Council of the city are open to the public and will be held in Kingwood City
Hall, located at 313 Tunnelton Street, Kingwood West Virginia 26537.
   (B)   Meeting notice. An official notice of all regular meetings of the
Council of the city will be posted on the front door of Kingwood City Hall
three business days prior to meeting day. For special meetings, two business
days' notice is required.
   (C)   Voting members. All duly elected officials of the city, Mayor,
Recorder and five Council members shall be voting members. The Mayor shall cast
his or her vote only after all other members of Council present have voted.
   (D)   Quorum. Four duly elected officials, a quorum, of the Council of the
city, must be present in order to conduct official business. It is permissible
for one or more official(s) to attend the meeting using a telecommunication
device, such as a cell phone, laptop or by video conferencing, however at least
one voting member of the Council shall be present at the statutory location for
each and every official Council meeting. If the Mayor is attending an official
meeting using a telecommunication device, the Recorder, if attending at the
statutory location, will conduct the meeting. If both the Mayor and the
Recorder are attending the meeting using a telecommunication device, then the
most senior member of the Council who is attending at the statutory location
will conduct the meeting.
   (E)   Presiding officers. The Mayor is the presiding officer for all
meetings of the Council of the city. In the absence of the Mayor, the Recorder
will be the presiding officer. If the Mayor and Recorder are both absent, then
the most senior member of the Council shall act as the presiding officer for
such meeting.
   (F)   Minutes. It is the responsibility of the Recorder to take the official
minutes of all meetings of the Council of the city. In the absence of the
Recorder, the City Clerk will be responsible for taking the official meeting
minutes.
(Ord. passed 7-8-2025)
CHAPTER 31: CITY OFFICIALS
Section
City Clerk
   
31.01   Generally
   
31.02   Qualifications
   
31.03   Responsibilities
CITY CLERK
§ 31.01 GENERALLY.
   The City Clerk is the connecting link between the City Council on the one
hand and the various boards of the city, city employees and general public on
the other hand.
   (A)   As City Treasurer, responsible for all funds of the city;
   (B)   Responsible to City Council;
   (C)   Responsible for maintaining all city records; and
   (E)   Must maintain a good relationship with the general public without
bending or allowing special favors due to friendship or for any other reason.
The same applies to City Council, the Mayor and Recorder, in so far as the
relationship is concerned.
§ 31.02 QUALIFICATIONS.
   (A)   High school graduate essential, college training preferred, along with
some business experience;
   (B)   Must develop a working knowledge of state and federal regulations,
which are different from general business in most cases; and
   (C)   Working knowledge of accounting and data processing needed.
§ 31.03 RESPONSIBILITIES.
   (A)   Issues building permits, checks applications for conformity to
Building and Zoning Codes. Take permit applications to Council;
   (B)   Sell cemetery lots and graves in Maplewood Cemetery, write deeds for
same, enter on cemetery maps, keep records for cemetery, including files;
   (C)   Keep Police Judge docket, collect all fines, send out letters to all
persons not paying fines or parking tickets, cause warrants to be issued when
required by ordinance. Send abstracts of judgement to Safety Responsibility
Division (Charleston);
   (D)   Issue and OK all purchase orders for the city;
   (E)   Issue all city licenses. Send out application forms for all city
licenses on June 1;
   (F)   Attend all Council meetings. Prepare agenda for Mayor. Prepare bills
and building permit applications for Council. Transcribe minutes into minute
book. Send out copies to Council;
   (G)   Prepare payroll checks, Deposit all moneys. Post all receipts and
disbursements. Write all checks for bills. Keeps all journals and ledgers
according to state requirements. Is Treasurer for the city;
   (H)   Send in all reports, such as Social Security, worker’s compensation,
employment security, federal and state income taxes, state sales tax, state
public retirement system, State Treasurer. Some are bi-monthly, some are
monthly, some are quarterly;
   (I)   Prepare annual budget and submit to Council. After Council approves,
submit State Tax Commissioner for approval. Make budget adjustments throughout
the fiscal year;
   (J)   Handles all city elections. Secures supplies, clerks and
commissioners, receives all filings and fees, handles absentee votes, all
according to the State Election Code. Prepare report of Canvassing Board;
   (K)   Handle annual city’s Halloween party;
   (L)   Treasurer of Park and Recreation Department by ordinance; and
   (M)   Secretary for Board of Zoning Appeals. Sets up meetings, takes minutes
and transcribes same.

BOARD OF WATER COMMISSIONERS
§ 32.01 MANAGEMENT AND CONTROL IN BOARD.
   The management and control of the municipal waterworks system of the city
shall be carried on by a Board of Water Commissioners created, appointed and to
perform the functions as hereinafter prescribed.
(Ord. 17, passed 8-14-2018)
§ 32.02 APPOINTMENT OF BOARD.
   (A)   (1)   Said Board of Water Commissioners shall consist of seven
Commissioners who shall be of outstanding reputation for ability and integrity.
They shall be appointed without regard to their political affiliations, but
with regard to their business and professional experience or standing as
citizens in the community. Two of said Commissioners appointed must reside in
the area previously served by the County Public Service District No. 2.
      (2)   (a)   The initial Commissioners and their respective terms of
office shall be: the five Water Commissioners presently serving on the Board of
Water Commissioners and said Commissioners shall complete their appointed terms
as previously appointed.
         (b)   The two new Commissioners to be appointed upon passage of this
subchapter shall be appointed as follows: one Commissioner shall be appointed
for a two-year term; and one Commissioner shall be appointed for a three-year
term. Said terms shall be considered as having started on the date of
appointment.
   (B)   The adoption of this section is made contingent upon the approval of
the County Commission and the State Public Service Commission for the
acquisition of the County Public Service District No. 2 by the city. This
section will not be in effect upon final approval of the acquisition has been
given by the State Public Service Commission.
   (C)   Upon the adoption of this section and the receipt of the final
approval of the State Public Service Commission, the Council of the city shall
appoint the two new Commissioners for the terms previously noted of two years
and three years. Following said appointments to the Board of Water
Commissioners, all future appointments shall be made according to this section
providing for the management, control and operation of the municipal waterworks
system of the city.
   (D)   In the event of any vacancy on the Board, due to death, retirement,
inability to serve or other given reason with the exception of the expiration
of a term of said Commissioner, such vacancy shall be filled by the person
selected by the majority vote of the Board of Water Commissioners serving at
the time the vacancy occurs. Upon selection of a person to fill said vacancy,
the Board of Water Commissioners shall notify the Council of the city of said
appointment. In the event of a vacancy on the Board due to the expiration of
the term of a Commissioner, such vacancy shall be filled by a person appointed
for a three-year term by the Council of the city. The Board of Water
Commissioners may submit recommendations of names of people to be appointed to
the Board of Water Commissioners. However, the final appointment shall rest
upon the Council of the city. In regard to the appointment of the two
Commissioners residing in the area previously served by the County Public
Service District No. 2, the County Commission may submit recommendations to the
Board of Water Commissioners the names of people to be appointed to the Board
for the Board’s consideration prior to the Board submitting its recommendations
for appointment to the City Council.
   (E)   From and after the date of the issuance of the waterworks revenue
bonds of said city, the provisions of this subchapter shall govern and control
in the administration and operation of the municipal waterworks system of said
city. All vacancies shall be filled for the unexpired term of the Commissioner
so vacating and all other appointments shall be for a term of three years. A
majority of said Board, at any meeting, shall constitute a quorum. The Board
shall adopt rules and by-laws to be reduced to writing for the time and place
of its meetings, the conduct thereof, and the operation of said waterworks.
(Ord. 17, passed 8-14-2018)
§ 32.03 ELIGIBILITY AND COMPENSATION OF BOARD.
   (A)   Five of the appointed Commissioners shall, as long as they remain
Commissioners, be residents and taxpayers of the city. Two of the appointed
Commissioners shall, as long as they remain Commissioners, reside in the area
previously served by County Public Service District No. 2. Any Commissioner
appointed to said Board of Commissioners shall be eligible for reappointment
upon the expiration of his or her term.
   (B)   Each Commissioner, with the exception of the person serving as
Chairperson of the Board, while so acting as Commissioner, shall receive
compensation for his or her services at the rate of $125 per meeting attended
as may be fixed from time to time by the City Council or by designation of time
by the Board, with a maximum compensation to any one Commissioner of $1,750 per
annum, and each appointed Commissioner shall be removable for cause by the
recorded vote of a majority of the members of the Council of said city after
hearing duly held. The person serving as Chairperson of the Board, while so
acting as Chairperson of the Board, shall receive compensation for his or her
services at the rate of $200 per meeting attended as may be fixed from time to
time by the Council of said city or by designation of time by the Board, with a
maximum compensation to the Chairperson of the Board of $2,800 per annum.
(Ord. 17, passed 8-14-2018)
§ 32.04 OFFICERS AND ATTENDANCE OF BOARD.
   At the first meeting of the Board of Water Commissioners and annually
thereafter upon the anniversary date of the first meeting, or at some other
date agreed upon, said Board of Water Commissioners shall organize by the
designation of one of the Commissioners to act as Chairperson and another to
act as Secretary. The Chairperson so designated shall preside at all meetings
when present and shall call special meetings, as need be, of the Board.
Provision shall be made for holding at least one regular meeting per month, of
which special notice need not be given. The Secretary shall keep a written
record of the proceedings of the Board, which shall be available for inspection
as are all other municipal records. Any appointed Commissioner failing to
attend four successive regular meetings without cause acceptable and approved
by the Board of Commissioners, shall be thereby automatically removed from
office and such vacancy filled as hereinbefore provided.
(Ord. 17, passed 8-14-2018)
§ 32.05 OPERATION OF WATERWORKS AND REVENUE THEREFROM.
   The said Board of Water Commissioners shall have full and complete
supervision, management and control of the municipal waterworks system of said
city, including the administration, maintenance, operation and extension
thereof. Any contracts for construction or purchase involving the sum of
$10,000 or more, and all contracts for fuel or electricity extending over a
period of 12 months or more shall be authorized and approved by the Council of
said city upon the recommendation of the Board of Water Commissioners. All
bills for water and water service shall be collected and accounted for by said
Board of Water Commissioners in the manner and form required by law and all
collections shall be deposited with the Treasurer of said city waterworks or
deposited as he or she may direct. The municipal waterworks system shall be
operated on a fiscal year basis, commencing on July 1 of each year and ending
on June 30 of each year. At least 30 days prior to the deadline for budget
preparation as set by the state of each year, the Board of Water Commissioners
shall cause to be prepared and adopted a detailed budget of the estimated
amounts of money to be collected, and the amounts and purposes for which
expenditures are to be made in connection with the operation of the waterworks
system for the next ensuing fiscal year, a signed copy of which budget shall be
filed with the City Clerk. No contracts affecting the waterworks system shall
be entered into, or any waterworks revenue bonds issued other than those
referred to in the preamble to the ordinances adopted in this subchapter, for
extensions, improvements or replacements without the recommendation and
approval of said Board of Water Commissioners. All disbursements for account of
such waterworks system shall be ordered paid out of the money collected and the
original revenues obtained from the sale of said bonds only upon approval of
said Board of Water Commissioners.
(Ord. 17, passed 8-14-2018)
§ 32.06 EMPLOYEES OF BOARD.
   The Board of Water Commissioners shall have the power to employ, fix the
compensation of and discharge a Superintendent, and through such
Superintendent, to direct, employ, fix the compensation of, and discharge all
employees of the Waterworks Department. The Superintendent shall perform such
duties as may be conferred upon him or her by the Board of Water Commissioners.
(Ord. 17, passed 8-14-2018)
§ 32.07 IN COMPLIANCE WITH STATE LAW.
   Nothing herein shall be construed to be done outside the scope of W. Va.
Code Ch. 8, Art. 12, §§ 1 to 14 relating to waterworks of municipal
corporations, and said chapter, articles and sections of said code shall be
complied with in the operation of the city waterworks.
(Ord. 17, passed 8-14-2018)
§ 32.08 BOND.
   All members of said Board of Water Commissioners, all employees of said city
waterworks, including the Superintendent thereof shall be bonded with corporate
surety in an amount at least equal to the amount of money coming into the hands
of said Board of Water Commissioners during each fiscal year; all employees
shall be covered and be placed under the scope of the worker’s compensation
laws of the state or other adequate means taken to save the city harmless by
reason of any act or thing done by the said Board of Water Commissioners or any
agent or employee thereof. The amount of such bonds herein provided for shall
be set from time to time by the Council of said City of Kingwood.
(Ord. 17, passed 8-14-2018)
SANITARY BOARD
§ 32.20 CREATION OF SANITARY BOARD.
   The Council of the city does hereby create and establish a Sanitary Board,
with all powers and duties as provided in and pursuant to W. Va. Code Ch. 16,
Art. 13.
(Ord. 34, passed 7-26-2016)
§ 32.21 COMPOSITION, CHAIRPERSON, APPOINTMENT OF MEMBERS.
   The Sanitary Board shall be composed of the Mayor of the city, and two
persons appointed by the Council, one of whom, during the construction period
of any sewer facilities, must be a registered professional engineer. The
engineer member of the Board need not be a resident of said municipality. After
the construction of the system has been completed, the engineer may be
succeeded by a person not an engineer. Said appointees shall originally be
appointed for terms of two and three years respectively, and upon the
expiration of each such term and each succeeding term, appointment of a
successor shall be made in like manner for a term of three years. Vacancies
shall be filled for an unexpired term in the same manner as the original
appointment. No officer or employee of the city, whether holding a paid or
unpaid office, shall be eligible to appointment on said Sanitary Board until at
least one year after the expiration of the term of his or her public office.
(Ord. 34, passed 7-26-2016)
§ 32.22 ORGANIZATIONAL MEETINGS, VICE CHAIRPERSON, SECRETARY, TREASURER,
OFFICIAL BONDS.
   As soon as may be practicable following the appointment of a new member of
the Sanitary Board, the Board shall hold an organizational meeting and choose a
Vice Chairperson from among its members, and a Secretary and Treasurer, who may
be one person and need not be a Board member, and such officers shall hold
office at the will of the Board. No bond shall be required of the Board members
as such, but the Treasurer, whether a member of the Board or not, shall give
bond in the penalty of $2,000 for the proper application of all money received
by him or her as Treasurer of the Board, and otherwise conditioned according to
law.
(Ord. 34, passed 7-26-2016)
§ 32.23 COMPENSATION AND EXPENSES OF BOARD MEMBERS.
   The members of the Sanitary Board as such shall be paid the amount of $50
per meeting attended by said Board member with a maximum number of meetings for
which payment may be made within a year being at the total of 16 meetings or a
yearly salary not to exceed the amount of $800. In addition, all members of the
Board shall be reimbursed from sewage works funds for all necessary expenses
properly incurred in the discharge of their duties, but there shall be no
liability upon the city for any salary or expenses so incurred.
(Ord. 34, passed 7-26-2016)
§ 32.24 POWERS, DUTIES AND LIMITATIONS.
   (A)   The Sanitary Board shall have the supervision and control of the
custody, administration, operation and maintenance of any and all works for the
collection, treatment and disposal of sewage, which are now owned or may
hereafter be acquired by the city.
   (B)   The Sanitary Board shall have power to take all steps and proceedings
and to make and enter into all contracts or agreements necessary or incidental
to the performance of its duties and the execution of the powers granted to
such Board under W. Va. Code Ch. 16, Art. 13 as the same now exists and may
hereafter be amended; but the powers of the Sanitary Board shall be subject to
all restrictions and limitations contained in said W. Va. Code Ch. 16, Art. 13
as the same now exists or may hereafter be amended.
   (C)   The Sanitary Board may employ engineers, architects, inspectors,
superintendents, a manager, collectors, attorneys and such other personnel as
in its judgement may be necessary in the execution of its powers and duties,
and may fix their compensation, all of whom shall do such work as the Board
shall direct. All such compensation and all expenses, incurred in carrying out
the provisions of W. Va. Code Ch. 16, Art. 13 shall be paid solely and only
from funds provided under the authority or power given it so as to bind the
Board or the city beyond the extent to which money shall have been or may be
provided under the authority of W. Va. Code Ch. 16, Art. 13. No contract or
agreement with any contractor or contractors for labor or material exceeding in
amount the sum of $5,000 or the maximum as provided by law shall be made
without advertising for bids, which bids shall be publicly opened and award
made to the best bidder, with power in the Board to reject any and all bids.
   (D)   The construction, acquisition, improvement, equipment, custody,
operation and maintenance of any such works for the collection, treatment or
disposal of sewage and the collection of revenues therefrom for the service
rendered thereby shall be under the supervision and control of the Sanitary
Board.
   (E)   After the construction, installation and completion of such works, the
Sanitary Board shall operate, manage and control the same and may order and
complete any extensions, betterments and improvement of and to the works that
the Board may deem expedient if funds therefor be available or made available
as provided by law, and shall establish rules and regulations for the use and
operation of the works and of other sewers and drains connected therewith so
far as they may affect the operation of such works, and to do all things
necessary or expedient for the successful operation thereof, and the Board
shall have in addition hereto any and all powers granted to it by said W. Va.
Code Ch. 16, Art. 13, or which may be granted to it by amendments to said W.
Va. Code Ch. 16, Art. 13, hereafter made, subject to any and all restrictions
and limitations therein contained.
(Ord. 34, passed 7-26-2016)
§ 32.25 DUTY OF BOARD TO RESTORE PROPERTY DAMAGED BY ITS ACTIVITIES.
   All public ways or public works damaged or destroyed by the Sanitary Board
in carrying out its authority under W. Va. Code Ch. 16, Art. 13 shall be
restored or repaired by the Board and placed in their original condition, as
nearly as practicable, if requested to do so by the proper authorities, out of
the funds provided pursuant to the provisions of W. Va. Code Ch. 16, Art. 13.
(Ord. 34, passed 7-26-2016)
§ 32.26 PUBLICATION OF FINANCIAL STATEMENT.
   The Sanitary Board shall prepare a financial statement and cause it to be
published as a Class I legal advertisement in compliance with the provisions of
W. Va. Code Ch. 59, Art. 3, and the publication area for such publication shall
be the sanitary district. Such statement shall contain an itemized account of
the receipts and expenditures of the Board during the previous fiscal year,
showing the source from which all money was derived, and the name of the person
to whom an order was issued, together with the amount of such order, and why
such order was issued, arranging the same under distinct heads, and including
all money received and expended from the sale of bonds, and also a specific
statement of the debts of such Board, showing the purpose for which any debt
was contracted, the amount of money in all funds at the end of the preceding
year, and the amount of uncollected service charges. Such statement shall be
prepared and published by the Board as soon as practicable after the close of
the fiscal year. The statement shall be sworn to by the Chairperson and
Secretary and Treasurer of the Board.
(Ord. 34, passed 7-26-2016)
§ 32.27 PROCEDURE FOR DISBURSEMENT OF FUNDS.
   All funds under the supervision of the Sanitary Board shall be disbursed, as
disbursements are required, by check drawn upon the proper fund or account, and
such checks shall be properly signed by the authorized officer or agent of the
Board. All such disbursements shall be approved by the Board.
(Ord. 34, passed 7-26-2016)
§ 32.28 BONDING OF EMPLOYEES WHO HANDLE MONEY.
   The Sanitary Board may from time to time, in its discretion, require any of
its employees to furnish a good and suitable indemnity bond, with a recognized
and reputable surety, conditioned upon the faithful discharge of their duties
as such, and to deliver up and pay over all money as provided by law. The Board
shall require all persons who collect of otherwise handle funds of the Board to
furnish a good and proper bond, with a recognized and reputable surety,
conditioned upon the faithful performance of their duties and for the proper
handling and care of said funds in their hands. Such bond shall be in an amount
equal to the sum of money which might at any one time be in the hands of such
person or persons, as may be determined by the Board.
(Ord. 34, passed 7-26-2016)
PLANNING COMMISSION
§ 32.40 GENERALLY.
   The city does hereby create a Planning Commission for the city to promote
the orderly development of its jurisdiction. Said Commission shall serve in an
advisory capacity to the governing body of the city and shall have certain
regulatory powers over land planning. The Planning Commission, along with the
governing body of this city, shall have the authority to carry out the
objectives and overall purposes of the W. Va. Code §§ 8A-1-1 et seq.
(Ord. passed 2-10-2009)
§ 32.41 MEMBERSHIP OF PLANNING COMMISSION.
   (A)   (1)   The Planning Commission shall have seven members.
      (2)   Each member must be:
         (a)   A resident of the municipality; and
         (b)   Qualified by knowledge and experience in matters pertaining to
the development of the municipality.
   (B)   At least three-fifths of all of the members must have been residents
of the municipality for at least three years prior to nomination or appointment
and confirmation.
   (C)   The members of the Planning Commission must fairly represent different
areas of interest, knowledge and expertise, including, but not limited to,
business, industry, labor, government and other relevant disciplines. Two
members must be a member of the municipal governing body (being one in the same
as administrative department) or a designee. One appointment represents the
governing body and the other represents the administrative department. The term
of membership for these two members is the same as their term of office.
   (D)   Should there be members of the community that may at times appear
before the Planning Commission and do have experience and expertise that would
be advantageous to the Commission, such act shall not be a conflict of interest
in the appointment to the Commission. If such person is appointed, this member
must recuse himself or herself from any vote, discussion, participation or
other activity regarding the conflicting issue.
   (E)   The remaining members of the Planning Commission first selected shall
serve respectively for terms of one year, two years and three years, divided
equally or as nearly equally as possible between these terms. Thereafter,
members shall serve three-year terms. Vacancies shall be filled for the
unexpired term and made in the same manner as original selections were made.
   (F)   The members of the Planning Commission shall serve without
compensation, but shall be reimbursed for all reasonable and necessary expenses
actually incurred in the performance of their official duties.
   (G)   Nominations for the Planning Commission membership shall be made and
confirmed by the governing body.
   (H)   Should any member of the Commission fail to attend meetings, neglect
his or her duties to the Commission or commit malfeasance of his or her
appointment, the Commission shall report such actions to the governing body.
Thereafter, the governing body shall provide written notice of such alleged
actions to the effected member and advise that such actions may result in the
member’s removal from the Commission. Should the member object, he or she shall
have an opportunity to address the governing body on the issues prior to any
final decision being made by the governing body.
(Ord. passed 2-10-2009)
§ 32.42 MEETINGS.
   (A)   The Planning Commission shall meet at least quarterly and may meet
more frequently at the request of the President or by two or more members.
   (B)   Notice for a special meeting must be in writing, include the date,
time and place of the special meeting, and be sent to all members at least two
days prior to the special meeting.
   (C)   Written notice of a special meeting is not required if the date, time
and place of the special meeting were set in a regular meeting.
   (D)   The Planning Commission must have quorum to conduct a meeting. A
majority of the members of a Planning Commission is a quorum. No action of a
Planning Commission is official unless authorized by a majority of the members
present at a regular or properly called special meeting.
(Ord. passed 2-10-2009)
§ 32.43 OFFICERS.
   At its first regular meeting each year, a Planning Commission shall elect
from its members a President and Vice President. The Vice President shall have
the power and authority to act as President of the Planning Commission during
the absence or disability of the President.
(Ord. passed 2-10-2009)
§ 32.44 GOVERNING BODY’S DUTIES.
   (A)   The city governing body shall provide the Planning Commission with:
      (1)   Suitable location for holding of meetings and the preservation of
plans, maps documents and accounts; and
      (2)   Appropriate money to defray the reasonable expenses of the Planning
Commission.
   (B)   The Planning Commission is authorized to accept gifts, funds and
donations which will be deposited with the appropriate governing body in a
special nonreverting Planning Commission Fund to be available for expenditures
by the Planning Commission for the purpose designated by the donor.
(Ord. passed 2-10-2009)
§ 32.45 POWERS AND DUTIES OF PLANNING COMMISSION.
   The Planning Commission has the following powers and duties:
   (A)   Exercise general supervision for the administration of the affairs of
the Commission;
   (B)   Prescribe rules and regulations pertaining to administration,
investigations and hearings; provided, that the rules and regulations are
adopted by the governing body;
   (C)   Supervise the fiscal affairs and responsibilities of the Commission;
   (D)   With consent from the governing body, hire employees necessary to
carry out the duties and responsibilities of the Planning Commission, provided
that the governing body sets the salaries;
   (E)   Keep an accurate and complete record of all Planning Commission
proceedings;
   (F)   Record and fill all bonds and contract;
   (G)   Take responsibility for the custody and preservation of all papers and
documents of the Planning Commission;
   (H)   Make recommendations to the governing body concerning planning;
   (I)   Make an annual report to the governing body concerning the operation
of the Planning Commission and the status of planning within its jurisdiction;
   (J)   Prepare, publish and distribute reports, ordinances and other material
relating to the activities authorized under this subchapter;
   (K)   Invoke any legal, equitable or special remedy for the enforcement of
the provisions of this subchapter, rule and regulation or any action taken
thereunder;
   (L)   Prepare and submit an annual budget to the governing body;
   (M)   Delegate limited powers to a Committee composed of one or more members
of the Commission; and
   (N)   Contract for special or temporary services and professional counsel
with the approval of the governing body.
(Ord. passed 2-10-2009)
BOARD OF PARKS AND RECREATION
§ 32.60 ESTABLISHMENT AND ORGANIZATION.
   (A)   Establishment of Board. There is hereby established a Board of Parks
and Recreation Commissioners for the city for the purpose of establishing,
constructing, improving, extending, developing, maintaining and operating a
city public park and recreation system. Its name shall be the "Board of Parks
and Recreation Commissioners of the City of Kingwood". For convenience of
reference herein, the Board of Parks and Recreation Commissioners of the city
will be hereinafter referred to as the "Board".
   (B)   Board a public corporate body; perpetual existence; and seal. The
Board created by this subchapter shall be a public corporate body, with
perpetual existence and a common seal.
   (C)   Members.
      (1)   The Board shall consist of five members, a majority of whom shall
constitute a quorum for the transaction of business, except as hereinafter
provided. Each member of the Board must be a resident and freeholder of the
city.
      (2)   The members of the Board shall be appointed by the Council. There
shall be at least one member of Council appointed to the Board at all times and
a second Council member may be appointed if Council so desires. Council
membership on the Board will be the same as their term of office on Council,
with reappointment after each election of new Council. The term of other
appointed members shall be for three years, and until their successors have
been duly appointed and qualified; provided, that in the initial appointment of
the members of the Board, Council shall appoint the three persons, who are not
members of Council, to serve, one for a term of six years, one for a term of
four years, and one for a term of two years. The date upon which the terms of
such Board members shall begin shall be July 1, 2025.
   (D)   Disqualification of member.
      (1)   When any member of the Board, during his term of office, shall
cease to be a resident and freeholder of the city, he shall thereby be
disqualified as a member of the Board and his office shall thereupon become
vacant.
      (2)   Any appointed Board member failing to attend three successive
regular meetings without cause acceptable by the Board, shall be thereby
automatically removed from office and such vacancy filled hereinbefore
provided.
   (E)   Filling vacancies. When a vacancy occurs on the Board by reason of
death, resignation, change of residence from the city, failure to remain a
freeholder of the city, or due to any other cause, the remaining member or
members of the Board shall appoint a successor or successors, or if there be no
members left on the Board, the Council shall appoint successors, and in either
event, the appointment shall be for the unexpired term or terms, provided,
however, that when the vacancy is that of a member of the Council, then Council
shall appoint such successor for the unexpired term.
   (F)   Oath of members. After appointment, the members of the Board shall
qualify by taking and filing with the Recorder of the city the oath prescribed
by law for public officials, and they shall not be permitted to serve upon said
Board until they have so qualified. If any member of the Board shall fail to so
qualify on or before the date upon which he should assume the duties of his
office, a vacancy shall exist which shall be filled as provided in division (E)
above.
   (G)   Organization of Board, Secretary, and Treasurer. At the first meeting
held after the first Board has been appointed, and thereafter on the 1st day of
December of each year, the members of the Board shall organize by election one
of their number Presidents, and another Vice-President, and by electing a
Secretary and Treasurer, who may be one person and need not be a Board member,
and such officers shall hold office at the will of the Board. The Secretary
shall keep an accurate record of all the fiscal affairs of the Board, and shall
keep a minute book in which he shall record the proceedings and transactions of
each meeting of the Board. The Treasurer shall take the oath prescribed by law
and shall furnish such bond as may be required by the Board.
   (H)   Members to be paid expenses. The members of the Board shall receive no
compensation for their services but they shall be entitled to reimbursement for
all reasonable and necessary expenses actually incurred in the performance of
their duties as members of the Board.
   (I)   Members not to be personally interested in contracts or property
controlled by Board. A member of the Board shall not be personally interested,
directly or indirectly, in any contract entered into by the Board, or hold any
remunerative position in connection with the establishment, construction,
improvement, extension, development, maintenance or operation of any of the
property under the control of the Board.
   (J)   Office. Council shall furnish the Board an office in the city building
where it may hold its meetings and keep its records.
(Ord. passed 6-10-2025)
§ 32.61 POWERS.
   (A)   General powers. The Board shall have the power to purchase, hold,
sell, and convey real or personal property; receive any gift, grant, donation,
bequest or devise, sue and be sued; contract and be contracted with; and do any
and all things and acts which may be necessary, appropriate, convenient or
incidental to carry out and effectuate the purposes and provisions of this
subchapter.
   (B)   Purchase, lease or condemnation of real property. The Board shall have
the power and authority to acquire in its name or in the name of the city by
purchase, lease, or by exercise of the power of eminent domain, or otherwise,
such land or lands as it shall determine to be necessary, appropriate,
convenient, or incidental to the establishment, construction, improvement,
extension, development, maintenance or operation of a system of public parks,
parkways, playgrounds, athletic fields, stadiums, swimming pools, skating
rinks, or arenas and other public park and recreational facilities for the
city, whether of a like or different nature.
   (C)   Authority to take title to real and personal property; conveyances of
real property to Board by public body; sales and conveyances of real property
by Board; and execution of deeds. The Board is hereby empowered and authorized
to take title in its name or in the name of the city to all real and personal
property acquired by it for the use of the public or useful to the public in
the establishment, construction, improvement, extension, development,
maintenance, or operation of all public parks, parkways, playgrounds, athletic
fields, stadiums, swimming pools, skating rinks or arenas and all other public
park and recreational facilities for the city, whether of a like or different
nature, and shall manage and dispose of the same as, in its opinion, will best
serve the interests of the public in carrying out the purposes of this section.
The city and all other public parks and recreation are hereby authorized to
convey the same to said Board to be held by it for such purposes, and said
Board is hereby authorized to receive the same. Nothing contained in this
subchapter shall be construed as limiting said Board from going beyond the
corporate limits of the city, anywhere within the state, to lease, purchase or
otherwise acquire any real property for the purposes herein set forth. The
Board shall have the right to sell and convey only such part of the real
property that it may acquire by gift, devise, or purchase or otherwise, as it
may determine to be of no advantage in the establishment, construction,
improvement, extension, development, maintenance or operation of said public
parks, parkways, playgrounds, athletic fields, stadiums, swimming pools,
skating rinks, or arenas and other public park and recreational facilities,
whether of a like or different naturel; except that the Board shall have the
power and authority to make such sales and conveyances of its real property as
may be necessary, appropriate or convenient to enable the city to obtain the
benefits of W.Va. Code Ch. 8, Art. 16, or any other similar acts or legislative
authorization. Under no circumstances shall any of such real property of the
Board be sold or conveyed except by unanimous vote of all the members of said
Board. All deeds conveying the real property of said Board shall be executed in
its official name by its President or Vice-President, shall have its seal
affixed and shall be duly attested by its Secretary.
   (D)   General powers of Board. The Board shall have the necessary,
appropriate, convenient and incidental powers and authority to manage and
control all public parks, parkways, playgrounds, athletic fields, stadiums,
swimming pools, skating rinks or arenas and other public park and recreational
facilities of all kinds used as a part of said public park and recreation
system or as a means of maintaining places of beauty, education, and
recreation, and promoting the health, property, lives, decency, morality and
good order of the general public, and particularly of the inhabitants of the
city and vicinity; to abate or cause to be abated all nuisances affecting same;
to regulate or prohibit the selling of any article, goods, wares or merchandise
within said park and recreation system so designated; to regulate or prohibit
the placing of signs, billboards, posters and advertisements within said park
and recreation system as so designated, or the grounds immediately adjacent
thereto; to have the same kept in good order and free from obstruction for the
use and benefit of the public; to restrict and prohibit vagrants, mendicants,
beggars, tramps, prostitutes or disorderly individuals therefrom to establish,
construct, improve, extend, develop, maintain and operate such parks, parkways,
playgrounds, athletic fields, stadiums, swimming pools, skating rinks or arenas
and other public park and recreational facilities, whether or a like or
different nature, on any grounds controlled by said Board; to acquire for
public use by lease or otherwise lands either within or without the corporate
limits of the city; to cause any public street, avenue, road, alley, way,
bridle path, or walkway, which is a part of the public park and recreation
system, to be graded, drained and surfaced; to construct, maintain and operate
all necessary sewers and water lines in connection with said public park and
recreation system; and to do any and all other things or acts which may in any
way be necessary, appropriate, convenient or incidental to the use and
enjoyment of said public park and recreation system by the general public as a
place or places of beauty, education, entertainment and recreation.
   (E)   Enactment and enforcement of rules and regulations; counsel. In order
to accomplish the purposes set forth in division (D) above, the Board is hereby
empowered and authorized to promulgate and amend from time to time such rules
and regulations as may be necessary, appropriate, convenient, or incidental
thereto; after codification of such rules and regulations, or any amendments
thereto, by ordinance of the Council which may provide penalties for a
violation thereof, which codification is hereby authorized, to enforce the same
by appropriate proceedings in any proper tribunal of this state, or any county,
district or municipality thereof; and to employ such police officers as it
shall deem necessary and proper. The City Attorney shall be the official
counsel for the Board and shall advise it on all legal matters, but the Board
may in its own discretion, employ other or additional counsel.
(Ord. passed 6-10-2025)
§ 32.62 FINANCING.
   (A)   Charges for use of recreational facilities; use of funds. The Board
may make reasonable charges to the public for the privilege of using any of the
recreational facilities provided in the park and recreation system and may use
the funds so received for the purpose of establishing, constructing, improving,
extending, developing, maintaining or operating said park and recreation
system.
   (B)   Use of city appropriation and other funds. In carrying out the
purposes of this subchapter, the Board is hereby empowered and authorized to
receive and disburse for such purposes, and moneys appropriated to it by the
Council, together with any other funds which may come into its hands by gift,
grant, donation, bequest, devise or from its operation or otherwise. Any
contracts or purchases for the sum of $35,000 or more shall be authorized and
approved by the Council of said city upon the recommendation of the Parks and
Recreation Board.
   (C)   Public parks and recreation bonds. The Board is empowered to recommend
to Council proposed capital improvement projects for the public parks and
recreational facilities of the city, and proposed financing thereof by the
issuance of bonds, in accordance with the provisions of W.Va. Code Ch. 8, Art.
21, § 13 and any other similar act or legislative authorization.
   (D)   Annual financial report. The Board shall submit to the Council on or
before September 1 of each year a detailed financial statement for the
preceding fiscal year of July 1 to June 30. Such report shall contain a
detailed record of all receipts and all disbursements. In addition, the Board
shall submit to Council from time to time such additional reports as Council
may request.
(Ord. passed 6-10-2025)
CHAPTER 33: ELECTIONS
Section
   
33.01   Election by ballot
   
33.02   Certificate of announcement
   
33.03   Filing fee
   
33.04   Elections in accordance with state law and residency requirements
   
33.05   Filing deadline
§ 33.01 ELECTION BY BALLOT.
   All elections hereinafter held for the election of city officers shall be by
the ballot system the same as state elections.
(Ord. 3, passed 1-24-1989)
§ 33.02 CERTIFICATE OF ANNOUNCEMENT.
   A certificate of announcement shall be filed, on behalf of all candidates
for city offices, with the City Recorder. Such certificate shall show the
office for which the candidate is filing, the name of the ticket he or she
represents, if any, his or her residence, number of ward and a statement of
eligibility to hold said office. Certificates of announcement forms shall be
furnished to all candidates by the City Recorder.
(Ord. 3, passed 1-24-1989)
§ 33.03 FILING FEE.
   Such candidate shall pay into the city treasury, at the time of filing his
or her certificate of announcement, the following fees:
 
For City Recorder     $8
For Mayor             $10
For member of Council $5
 
(Ord. 3, passed 1-24-1989)
§ 33.04 ELECTIONS IN ACCORDANCE WITH STATE LAW AND RESIDENCY REQUIREMENTS.
   All elections hereafter held, shall be held in accordance with the W. Va.
Code Ch. 8, Art. 5, relating to election, appointment, qualification and
compensation of officers; general provisions, relating to officers and
employees; elections and petitions generally; and conflict of interests. The
municipality does by this chapter elect to establish residency requirement for
any elected officer to be that said elected officer must have resided within
the municipality boundary limits for a period of at least 30 days preceding his
or her election.
(Ord. 3, passed 1-24-1989)
§ 33.05 FILING DEADLINE.
   Such certificate of nomination, together with the filing fee therefor, shall
be filed with the City Recorder at least 80 days prior to the election. All
tickets and names of candidates not thus filed, and the filing fee so paid,
shall not appear on the official ballot.
(Ord. 3, passed 1-24-1989)
