DEVELOPMENT, CONSTRUCTION AND REPLACEMENT OF SIDEWALKS
§ 94.01 INCORPORATION OF STATE LAW.
   (A)   By adoption of this subchapter, there is incorporated herein and made
a part hereof all sections of W. Va. Code Ch. 8, Art. 18, §§ 1 through 22
(inclusive), as may be applicable in regard to the building and renewal of
sidewalks.
   (B)   All building and renewal of sidewalks built in accordance with the
aforereferenced chapter of the West Virginia Code, and further all sidewalks
built or renewed within the municipality by any person, firm, business,
partnership or corporation, shall be built, repaired or renewed in accordance
with the following specifications as set forth herein.
(Ord. 30, passed 7-23-1985; Ord. 30, passed 7-27-1999)
§ 94.02 SPECIFICATIONS FOR SIDEWALK CONSTRUCTION AND RENEWAL.
   (A)   Generally.
      (1)   All applicable provisions of the general conditions and other
portions of the contract documents are a part of and govern work under this
section.
      (2)   (a)   All work shall be the responsibility of the general
contractor.
         (b)   The work in this contract shall, in general, consist of, but not
be limited to, the following:
            1.   Formwork;
            2.   Poured in place concrete; and
            3.   Tear out old walks and dispose of them in a workmanlike
manner.
   (B)   Cement. Cement shall be air entrained portland cement-Type 1A.
      (1)   Aggregates.
         (a)   Fine aggregates. Sand shall consist of grains of sand, free from
deleterious material; and
         (b)   Coarse aggregate. Shall be hard, durable, uncoated crushed
stone.
      (2)   Mixing water. Water shall be clean, taken from a source suitable
for domestic use.
   (C)   Concrete reinforcement.
      (1)   Reinforcement. Reinforcing shall meet the following requirements:
         (a)   Welded wire fabric reinforcing. Steel wire shall be spot welded
at intersections and of size indicated. No. 10 gauge, six by six inch wire mesh
shall be used as shown on prints; or
         (b)   Fiberglass reinforcing.
            1.   In the alternative, the concrete shall be mixed with
fiberglass.
            2.   The ratio of the mixture shall be one pound of fiberglass per
one yard of concrete.
   (D)   Mixing concrete.
      (1)   General. Except as otherwise specified, concrete shall be ready-
mixed or job mixed at the contractors option, and with the requirements of the
American Concrete Institute Building Code.
      (2)   Job-mixed concrete. Mix all concrete in an approved, batch type,
mechanical mixer equipped with water measuring and timing devices.
      (3)   The city will require six tests, three cylinders each, at city time
scheduling and at contractors expense for every 40 yards of concrete.
   (E)   Transporting concrete. Concrete shall be conveyed from mixer to place
of final deposit by the most expedient means to avoid separation of aggregates,
setting of mixture of loss of material.
   (F)   Concrete formwork. All forming work is to comply with recommended
practice of concrete forming.
   (G)   Relocations.
      (1)   The city will remove all parking meters where sidewalks are to be
placed.
      (2)   The city will furnish three-inch sleeves to be anchored and
installed in concrete by the contractor.
      (3)   The contractor will work with the water company, gas company, city
or any utility company, for raising or lowering meters, values, lines and the
like.
   (H)   Strength and consistency.
      (1)   Strength.
         (a)   Except as otherwise specified, concrete shall have the
compressive strength at seven days and 28 days.
         (b)   Compressive strength of all concrete, for all walks, shall be
3,500 pound concrete.
      (2)   Exposed concrete. Exposed concrete, all walks, shall contain 5%,
plus or minus one, entrained air through the use of air intrained cement, or an
air entrained admixture conforming to A.S.T.M.
      (3)   Required. All concrete to be 3,500 pound concrete.
   (I)   Removal of forms. Forms shall be removed in a workmanlike manner, so
not to chip or damage concrete in any way.
   (J)   Concrete walks.
      (1)   Concrete walks shall consist of poured concrete, four inches
minimum depth, with a broom finish across the short direction of walk with
tooled edge.
      (2)   The concrete shall be screened to proper elevation. While concrete
is still plastic, the surface shall be floated with wood, cork or metal float.
      (3)   The subgrade shall be uniformly grazed and four inches of clean
three-fourths-inch stone.
      (4)   Provide one-half inch expansion (one-half inch by four-inch
asphalt) at entrance platforms, steps, intersection, with driveway or street
sidewalks, and at the changes of walk widths.
      (5)   A ramp of a maximum height of 30 degrees must be at all crosswalks
and said ramp shall be one and one-half times the width of a wheelchair or the
width of the sidewalk, whichever is greater.
   (K)   (1)   Below are design drawings, which more accurately, by picture,
explain and illustrate specific requirements of this subchapter for all
sidewalks built or renewed within the municipality, and said drawings shall be
adhered to as though they are set forth in writing within this subchapter.
      (2)   The Supervisor of City Services shall have the authority to alter
the design on specific requirements of this subchapter upon his or her
determination that abnormal circumstances exist.
[https://export.amlegal.com/media/ab40f3c6294e0f64503f8145f44a4f32ffe0bb46/
IMAGES/0-0-0-1531.png]
[https://export.amlegal.com/media/ab40f3c6294e0f64503f8145f44a4f32ffe0bb46/
IMAGES/0-0-0-1533.png]
(Ord. 30, passed 7-23-1985; Ord. 30, passed 7-27-1999)
§ 94.03 NOTICE TO PROPERTY OWNER OF NEEDED WORK.
   All spot repair work which may be performed by the municipality or persons,
firm, business, partnership or corporation abutting said sidewalk, shall be in
accordance with the specifications of this subchapter and shall match the
existing work and grade of said existing sidewalk.
(Ord. 30, passed 7-23-1985; Ord. 30, passed 7-27-1999)
§ 94.04 ENFORCEMENT.
   (A)   Prior to the Council of said municipality adhering to the
specifications of the West Virginia Code, as hereinbefore referred to, said
Council shall cause to be mailed a written notice to all abutting property
owners who abut to the area in which the Council has determined that the
present sidewalk should be renewed or repaired, and said notice shall be sent
by United States mail to the owner of said abutting property at said owner’s
last known address. Said notice shall contain the fact that the Council has
determined that the sidewalk abutting said property owner is in need of renewal
or repair and that a discussion of such will be held on a specific date of a
regular Council meeting. Further, said notice shall state that the owner may
voluntarily renew or repair said sidewalk, if done in accordance with the
provisions of this subchapter under the supervision of the Supervisor of City
Services. Said notice shall further advise the property owner that should said
property owner fail to voluntarily agree to make such renewal or repairs, that
the Council will consider an ordinance mandating said repairs, in accordance
with the West Virginia Code. Said notice provided for by this section shall be
prior to any action taken, as provided for by the W. Va. Code Ch. 8, Art. 18.
   (B)   It shall be the responsibility of the municipality, Supervisor of City
Services, to enforce this subchapter in regard to the specifications of the
construction or renewal of any sidewalk within the municipality. Upon said
Supervisor observing that a sidewalk within the municipality has not been built
or repaired in accordance with the proper specifications herein contained, the
Supervisor shall cause to be served, by written notice, either personally
served or mailed by the United States mail upon the person so constructing or
repairing said sidewalk, and upon the abutting property owner upon the person
responsible for having said sidewalk built or repaired, and that said notice
shall make said persons aware that the sidewalk is not being built or repaired
in accordance with the specifications of the municipality, and that said
construction shall be stopped immediately until such time as the specifications
of the municipality have been incorporated within the plans for said sidewalk.
   (C)   Should the Supervisor, upon notice being received by the appropriate
person, firm, business, corporation or partnership, observe that said notice is
not being adhered to, then said Supervisor shall have the responsibility and
authority to seek an injunction against said person, firm, business,
corporation or partnership, to enforce the specifications of this subchapter.
   (D)   It is further ordained that this subchapter shall apply to all
sidewalks that are so developed and repaired within the municipal corporation.
(Ord. 30, passed 7-23-1985; Ord. 30, passed 7-27-1999) Penalty, see §
94.99
CONSTRUCTION AND MAINTENANCE OF CITY STREETS
§ 94.15 CLEARING; TREE REMOVAL AND GRUBBING.
   (A)   All trees and stumps shall be removed from said roadway or street area
which is within the construction site, which site includes the roadway,
drainage area and all appurtenant area thereto in regard to the building and
maintenance of said roadway. Trees, shrubs and the like that could be hazardous
within said construction site right-of-way may be removed upon the direction
and approval of the Supervisor of City Services.
   (B)   In the building of a new roadway, the topsoil shall be removed to a
minimum of eight inches depth.
(Ord. 31, passed 5-24-1994)
§ 94.16 EXCAVATING AND GRADING.
   (A)   During the cut and fill operation of said roadway-construction, all
existing and new utility lines shall be protected from any damage by the
contractor.
   (B)   There shall be removed from the construction site of said roadway all
unsuitable soils, debris and all excess material that may be harmful, damaging
or inappropriate in the construction of said roadway.
   (C)   Said roadway shall be appropriately graded to remove all unnecessary
bumps, hills, dips and other such problems which are not advantageous to the
building of an appropriate roadway.
   (D)   All wet weather springs or wet conditions of any kind which are
discovered within the construction site of said roadway must be dug out, water
piped to permit appropriate drainage and said area filled with stone and
compacted in a proper way.
   (E)   The grades of said roadway shall be uniform levels or slopes between
elevation points or existing grades and shall consider driveways, existing
roadways and other pertinent points in determining the location and grade of
the newly constructed roadway.
   (F)   Engineering designs for said roadway shall indicate elevation points;
however, should certain points not be indicated, then said grades shall be
directed by the Supervisor of City Services.
(Ord. 31, passed 5-24-1994)
§ 94.17 BASE AND BITUMINOUS MIX.
   (A)   The base of said roadway shall consist of two-inch stone (in size) and
three-inch stone (in size) compacted to a minimum of six inches in depth.
Following the compacting of the two-inch and three-inch stone, there shall be a
layer of one-half-inch stone (in size) crusher run to a depth of one inch to
fill all voids in said roadway.
   (B)   The hot laid asphaltic base shall be of a minimum of two and one-half
inches compacted over the base described in division (A) above.
   (C)   A hot laid asphaltic wearing course placed on top of the hot laid
asphaltic base shall be a minimum of one and one-half inches compacted.
   (D)   All compaction of items hereinbefore referred to be compacted shall be
done with a minimum of a ten-ton tandem roller.
(Ord. 31, passed 5-24-1994)
§ 94.18 REPAVING OF STREETS.
   (A)   When any soft areas become apparent or any part of the pavement
becomes badly broken and loose, such area must be dug out and removed from the
said roadway.
   (B)   Such areas which are dug out and removed must be filled and properly
compacted with stone to a depth of three inches below the top of the existing
pavement.
   (C)   The area between the three inches below the top of the existing
pavement must then be filled with asphaltic concrete and may be laid with the
top layer or wearing course.
   (D)   All repavement shall be done with hot asphaltic wearing course
compacted to two inches.
   (E)   All compaction herein referred to must be compacted with a minimum of
a ten-ton tandem roller.
(Ord. 31, passed 5-24-1994)
§ 94.19 ENGINEERING DESIGN.
   (A)   An engineering design shall be developed for all new roadways built in
accordance with this subchapter.
   (B)   Said design shall include the width of said roadway, the drainage
area, the grade elevations and shall illustrate that the minimum of the
requirements herein stated are met within said design for the paving of said
roadway.
   (C)   Said design shall further include a turning radius on all roadways,
which said radius shall be one-half of the width of the road which shall
actually be designed as being a point located at the turning corner which is
one-half of the road width away from each of said roads on either side of the
turn. Once said point is determined, then perpendicular lines shall be
established to each of said roads to determine a point upon said roadway. An
arch shall then be established between said two points to provide the turning
radius on each roadway.
(Ord. 31, passed 5-24-1994)
§ 94.20 AUTHORITY OF SUPERVISOR OF STREET SERVICES.
   (A)   The Supervisor of City Services shall have the right to make all
necessary changes at the roadway construction site as may be necessary due to
specific circumstances that may arise following the beginning of said
construction, provided that said changes are minor changes in regard to this
subchapter.
   (B)   Should the Supervisor find that major changes are required due to
specific circumstances in the construction of said roadway, said Supervisor
shall present said major change to the Council of said municipality for
approval in the engineering design of the change as required.
(Ord. 31, passed 5-24-1994)
USE OF STREETS AND SIDEWALKS
§ 94.35 POLES AND WIRES AS OBSTRUCTIONS TO STREET.
   It shall be the duty of all telephone, telegraph, cable and electric
companies, and any other person, firm or corporation to remove and reset
telephone, telegraph and other poles and wires connected therewith when the
same constitute an obstruction to the use of the streets by the traveling
public.
(Ord. 11, passed 8-23-1983) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.36 REQUIREMENT OF PERMIT.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to tunnel under or
to make any excavation in any street, alley or other public place in the city
without having obtained a permit as in herein required, or without complying
with the provisions of this subchapter or in violation of or variance from the
terms of any such permit.
(Ord. 11, passed 8-23-1983) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.37 APPLICATION FOR PERMITS.
   Applications for such permits shall be made to the Clerk, and shall describe
the location of the intended excavation or tunnel, the size thereof, the
purpose therefor and the person, firm or corporation doing the actual
excavating work in the name of the person, firm or corporation for whom or
which the work is being done, and shall contain an agreement that the applicant
will comply with all ordinances and laws relating to the work to be done.
(Ord. 11, passed 8-23-1983)
§ 94.38 COMPLIANCE WITH PERMIT.
   It shall be unlawful to make any excavation or tunnel in any way contrary to
or at variance with the terms of the permit therefor. No injuries shall be done
to any pipes, cables or conduits in the making of such excavations or tunnels;
and notice shall be given to the persons maintaining any such pipes, cables or
conduits or to the city department or officer charged with the care thereof,
which are or may be endangered or affected by the making of any such excavation
or tunnel before such pipes, cables or conduits shall be disturbed. No
unnecessary damage or injury shall be done to any tree or shrub or the roots
thereof.
(Ord. 11, passed 8-23-1983) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.39 OBSTRUCTION OR DAMAGE TO SIDEWALKS.
   If any sidewalk is blocked by any such work, a temporary sidewalk shall be
constructed or provided which shall be safe for travel and convenient for
users. Whenever any section of sidewalk is broken or busted during the course
of excavation, tunneling or the removing and resetting of poles, then the
complete section of the sidewalk so broken or busted will be replaced in such
manner and form as to be equal (or better) to the quality and quantity of the
section replaced.
(Ord. 11, passed 8-23-1983)
§ 94.40 RESTORATION OF WORK AREA.
   Any person, firm or corporation making any excavation or tunnel in or under
any public street, alley or other public place in the city shall restore the
surface to its original condition if there is no pavement there. Refills shall
be properly tapped down, and any bracing in such tunnel or excavation shall be
left in the ground.
(Ord. 11, passed 8-23-1983)
§ 94.41 REPLACEMENT OF PAVED OR IMPROVED STREET.
   (A)   Any opening in any paved or improved portion of a street shall be
repaired and the surface replaced by the applicant under the supervision of the
Supervisor of City Service in accordance with the following requirements:
      (1)   Backfill shall be of selected granular material such as concrete
sand or fine aggregate free of large lumps, clods or rock, and shall be
moistened before compaction if required by the engineer. Special care shall be
taken to thoroughly compact the material under the haunches of the pipe by
bringing the fill up evenly on both sides of the pipe for it full strength.
This fill shall continue until the fill is level with the top of pipe. At this
point, backfill shall be placed in even successive four inch layers not
exceeding four inches in depth and thoroughly compacted with improved
mechanical tamper. Any nonmetallic pipe shall have a tracer wire laid with the
pipe.
      (2)   All excess debris and materials will be removed and immediate area
will be cleared in a manner to be approved by the Supervisor of City Services.
The pavement shall be replaced in successive layers of compacted fill to top of
trench followed with four inches of 2500 portland concrete and two inches of
compacted bituminous wearing course surface, moistened and compacted with a
pneumatic tamper.
   (B)   The cutting of the pavement, the backfilling, and the replacing of the
pavement shall be done in accordance with the requirements detailed in the
figure below, dated August 1, 1983.
[https://export.amlegal.com/media/ab40f3c6294e0f64503f8145f44a4f32ffe0bb46/
IMAGES/0-0-0-1535.png]
(Ord. 11, passed 8-23-1983)
§ 94.42 APPLICATION TO DRIVEWAYS.
   The provisions of this subchapter shall apply to any driveways as well as
city streets.
(Ord. 11, passed 8-23-1983)
§ 94.43 LIABILITY TO COSTS INCURRED BY CITY.
   Any excavation or tunneling that is not replaced in accordance with the
terms of this subchapter may be done by the city at the cost and expense of the
person, firm or corporation for whom said excavation or tunneling was done. The
imposing of any fine under the terms of this subchapter shall not operate as a
release or relieve in any manner the responsibility of the replacement of the
pavement of surface in accordance with the requirements of this subchapter.
(Ord. 11, passed 8-23-1983)
§ 94.44 USE OF MACHINERY WITH TRACKS OR METAL CLEATS.
   Any machinery with tracks or metal cleats or braces used in any such
excavation or tunneling shall have rubber mounts or blocks under such tracks,
cleats and braces.
(Ord. 11, passed 8-23-1983)
STREET NUMBERS
§ 94.55 DISPLAY REQUIRED.
   (A)   The Post Office has requested that the property within the city be
numbered for mail delivery purposes. The Council of the city finds that the
numbering of and the displaying of numbers upon property for location purposes
would be beneficial to the municipality.
   (B)   All real estate located within the limits of the municipality shall be
given a number identifying the specific residence or building located upon said
real estate as located upon specific streets and all of said assigned numbers
shall be displayed upon residences and buildings located within the
municipality.
(Ord. 35, passed 4-12-1966)
§ 94.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter, for which no other
penalty is provided, shall be subject to the penalty provisions of §
10.99.
   (B)   Any person, firm or corporation violating any of the provisions of §§
94.35 through
94.44 shall be fined not more than $100 for a first offense, and for a second
or subsequent offense occurring within a 12-month period shall be fined not
less than $100 or more than $500. A separate offense shall be deemed committed
on each day during or on which a violation occurs or continues.
(Ord. 11, passed 8-23-1983)
CHAPTER 95: MAPLEWOOD CEMETERY
Section
   
95.01   Cost of opening and closing graves
   
95.02   Selling and price of grave lots
   
95.03   Requirement of outside burial container
   
95.04   Special section for burial of cremation remains
   
95.05   Requirement of marker foundation
   
95.06   Perpetual care fund
§ 95.01 COST OF OPENING AND CLOSING GRAVES.
   (A)   The opening and closing of regular adult internment spaces (i.e.
graves) within said Maplewood Cemetery shall be conducted by the employees of
the city for which charges will be set by the city and said charges shall be
paid for in advance of the opening of a grave by an individual or by a funeral
director. The cost for said opening and closing by the city shall be in the
amount of $600 for each opening and closing of a regular adult burial grave,
with the exceptions as hereinafter identified. The grave site is dug as six
feet deep, four feet wide and eight feet long.
   (B)   The opening and closing of other grave sites shall follow all
guidelines set forth herein in regard as to who opens the grave and how charges
are to be paid; however, charges for graves other than regular adult grave
sites are to be charged as follows:
      (1)   Opening and closing for an infant container up to 42 inches is the
amount of $400 with a grave site dug as three feet deep, two feet wide and
three and one-half feet long;
      (2)   Opening and closing for an oversized casket and container is $700
with a grave site dug as necessary; and
      (3)   Opening and closing for cremation remains is $300.
   (C)   Should the burial in the cemetery occur after 3:00 p.m. on a week day,
there shall be an additional charge of $200 added to each opening and closing
cost as set forth above to account for this special time of burial.
   (D)   Should the burial in the cemetery occur on the days of Saturday,
Sunday and/or Monday there shall be an additional charge of $275 added to each
opening and closing cost as set forth above to account for this special time of
burial. Monday is included as a special time of burial since the opening of the
grave for a Monday burial will have to occur over the weekend when city offices
are closed. Should the burial in the cemetery occur on certain holidays, being
days that the offices of the city are closed for a specific named holiday,
there shall be an additional charge of $275 added to each opening and closing
cost to account for this special day of burial.
   (E)   In addition to the payment of the cost of the opening and closing of
the grave site together with any applicable additional costs, the owner of the
grave site or his or her authorized representative or a representative of the
funeral home handling the burial shall execute an authorization and release for
interment. This document describes the location of the burial plot and places
responsibility for ascertaining the location thereof on the owner or his or her
representative. This executed document must be presented to the city at the
time that the burial costs are paid. The city will not open a grave lot prior
to obtaining an executed authorization and release for interment. A copy of
said authorization is adopted by reference and made a part thereof as if set
out in full herein.
(Ord. 29, passed 3-27-2018)
§ 95.02 SELLING AND PRICE OF GRAVE LOTS.
   (A)   The Maplewood Cemetery has been mapped and plotted into individual
lots be separate divisions of the cemetery, which said divisions and plots have
been platted and are of record in the City Clerk’s office, and that said
individual lots in said cemetery are available to be purchased by any
individual, firm or corporation and that each said lot shall sell for the price
of $500 each.
   (B)   The Clerk of the city shall, upon selling a lot or lots of said
Maplewood Cemetery prepare a deed of conveyance for said cemetery lot, which
said deed shall be under the supervision of the City Attorney and shall be
executed by the Mayor of said city to convey clear title to said cemetery lot
to the purchaser of said lot.
(Ord. 29, passed 3-27-2018)
§ 95.03 REQUIREMENT OF OUTSIDE BURIAL CONTAINER.
   It is herein provided that an outside burial container must be used for all
burials within the Maplewood Cemetery. It shall be the rule and regulation of
the Maplewood Cemetery that only a cement box, cement or steel vault, or other
vault built of a reasonable facsimile shall be used as an outer burial
container within the Maplewood Cemetery. There shall not be permitted any
wooden box to be used as an outer burial container.
(Ord. 29, passed 3-27-2018)
§ 95.04 SPECIAL SECTION FOR BURIAL OF CREMATION REMAINS.
   (A)   Maplewood Cemetery shall maintain a special section within the
cemetery for the burial of cremation remains.
   (B)   Said individual cremation lots in said cemetery are available to be
purchased by any individual, firm or corporation and that each said lot shall
sell for the price of $250 each.
   (C)   The Clerk of the city shall, upon selling a lot or lots of said
Maplewood Cemetery, prepare a deed of conveyance for said cemetery lot, which
said deed shall be under the supervision of the City Attorney and shall be
executed by the Mayor of said city to convey clear title to said cemetery lot
to the purchaser of said lot.
(Ord. 29, passed 3-27-2018)
§ 95.05 REQUIREMENT OF MARKER FOUNDATION.
   Any person or entity who owns a lot in the Maplewood Cemetery and does
desire to place a marker upon said lot identifying the grave site shall notify
the city of the type of marker to be used, the size and such other information
as the city may request. A foundation for all grave markers shall be required
to be built by the grave marker company in accordance with the requirements of
the marker. Any company desiring to set a grave marker shall give a minimum
notice of 48 hours prior to the date that the company intends to set the grave
marker. Prior to a company entering the cemetery to set the grave marker, the
representative of the company shall visit City Hall and identify himself or
herself so that a representative of the city may accompany the marker company
to the cemetery and specifically identify the grave site. A representative of
the city must be present to inspect the grave marker foundation hole prior to
any pouring for the marker foundation. No marker company may pour a marker
foundation, unless it is approved by a representative of the city.
(Ord. 29, passed 3-27-2018)
§ 95.06 PERPETUAL CARE FUND.
   Upon the sale of a burial lot, cremation or regular lot, 10% of the purchase
price of said burial lot shall be deposited into the perpetual care fund for
the cemetery and expenditures from said fund shall be only in accordance to the
cemetery rules and statutes as set forth in the West Virginia State Code and
mandated to be followed by all owners of cemeteries.
(Ord. 29, passed 3-27-2018)
CHAPTER 96: YARD AND GARAGE SALES
Section
   
96.01   Definitions
   
96.02   Registration required
   
96.03   Fee
   
96.04   Certificate
   
96.05   Period and place of sale
   
96.06   Revocation
   
96.99   Penalty
§ 96.01 DEFINITIONS.
   The terms YARD SALE, GARAGE SALE, FLEAMARKET and ISOLATED TRANSACTION as
used in this chapter shall have one in the same meaning and reference and shall
include any activity whereby an individual or individuals, company or
corporation shall place for sale to the public in public places and on private
property and not from an established business on private property miscellaneous
new and used items at a monetary charge for which there is no state tax charged
and for which a sale or business license has not been obtained and sales tax is
not collected nor reported. Such sale is an isolated incident, not occurring on
a regular or scheduled arrangement and the seller is not in the business of
selling the type of tangible personal property offered for sale.
(Ord. passed 5-9-2006)
§ 96.02 REGISTRATION REQUIRED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person or organization to engage in the
activity of yard sales, garage sales, fleamarkets, or other isolated
transactions without first having registered in the office of the City Clerk
and having obtained a permit for such activity. Such registration must occur at
least two days prior to the operation of such activity. The registrant shall
give his/her complete identification; the identification of all individuals,
companies and corporations included and participating in or contributing to the
sale; the applicant’s signature; nature of sale; and the actual physical
location of said sale with the street address and property owners’ full names.
(Ord. passed 5-9-2006)
§ 96.03 FEE.
   A fee of $5 per day shall be charged for such sale registration.
(Ord. passed 5-9-2006)
§ 96.04 CERTIFICATE.
   Each applicant who appropriately applies and provides the necessary
information to the City Clerk shall be furnished a certificate indicating that
he or she has registered and showing the date such yard sale or the like is
authorized and the authorized site of said sale. Each applicant shall have at
the sale the registration certificate and the same shall be exhibited by such
registrant whenever he/she is required to do so by any police officer or by any
other authorized personnel. No applicant shall be issued a certificate for such
sale in his/her name for sales exceeding two days in any one calendar year. The
certificate issued may be for four one day sales or two two day sales or
whatever arrangement of four days of sales the applicant may request, but in no
circumstance shall certificate(s) be issued for more than a total of four days
of total days of sale per year. No person shall individually receive a
certificate for a sale which exceeds a cumulative of four days in each calendar
year. Further, the site of the sale may have a certificate(s) for only a
cumulative of four days in any one calendar year and no site shall be the
location of a sale which exceeds this time limitation. No certificate shall be
issued to any applicant who has an outstanding unpaid fine in regard to prior
violations of this chapter and such certificate shall be withheld until such
outstanding fines are paid in full.
(Ord. passed 5-9-2006)
§ 96.05 PERIOD AND PLACE OF SALE.
   The authorized period of the sale as herein registered shall not exceed four
days in any one calendar year and will be confined between the hours of 8:00
a.m. and 6:00 p.m. of each day. Only certificates for four sale days will be
issued for the same site and location of sale in any one calendar year and the
issue of a change of ownership of the site or change of tenant shall not alter
this requirement. No sign for said yard sale or the like shall be placed on any
utility pole, street light poles, street signs or road signs. All signs posted
in other areas shall be removed within 24 hours of the completion of the yard
sale.
(Ord. passed 5-9-2006)
§ 96.06 REVOCATION.
   Any such registration and certificate may be revoked by the Mayor or the
Chief of Police because of any violation by the registrant of this chapter or
of any other ordinance of the city or of any state or federal law, or whenever
the registrant shall cease to possess the qualifications and character required
in this chapter for a certificate to be issued.
(Ord. passed 5-9-2006)
§ 96.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person who is guilty of a violation of any provision of this
chapter, upon conviction thereof, shall be fined not less than $10 nor more
than $500 for each offense and each offense shall be deemed committed on each
day during on or which a violation occurs or continues. Such fine is applicable
to the person holding such permit and violating the provisions set forth herein
and, further, said fine is applicable to any individual who fails to secure
such a certificate prior to having said yard sale. The Kingwood Police, upon
observing a yard sale occurring which does not have a certificate, shall issue
a cease and stop order and force the yard sale to shut down. The violation
shall be reported and hearing held at which time a fine may thereafter be
issued.
   (B)   Should any yard sale, or the like, sign be placed on a utility pole,
street light pole or on road signs, the person obtaining the certificate shall
be fined $50 per sign posted in said locations.
(Ord. passed 5-9-2006)
TITLE XI: BUSINESS REGULATIONS
   Chapter
      
110.   BUSINESS LICENSES
      
111.   ALCOHOL

113.   NUDE DANCING
CHAPTER 110: BUSINESS LICENSES
Section
   
110.01   Business licenses; generally
 
   
110.99   Penalty
§ 110.01 BUSINESS LICENSES; GENERALLY.
   (A)   By virtue of the adoption of this section, there is hereby imposed an
annual license tax upon various business classifications operating within the
municipality, and, following the effective date of this section, no person may
engage in a business in a capacity falling within the business classifications
itemized in the list below within the corporate limits of the city, without
first obtaining a license from the city, nor shall a person continue to engage
in such activity after his or her license has expired, been suspended or
revoked.
   (B)   The city shall collect an annual fee per year for the license issued
under this section as follows. The annual fee shall be assessed in accordance
with business classifications as defined under W. Va. Code Ch. 11, Art. 12, as
amended, which said various classifications and the rate to be charged for each
annual fee is shown and identified in the attached itemized business
classifications listing, to which said reference is hereby made and said list
is hereby incorporated herein as though set forth in its complete entirety
within this section.
   (C)   The license period shall begin on July 1 of each year commencing July
1, 2021 and ending on June 30 of the following year, and if the initial license
is granted for less than a year, the fee shall be computed in proportion to the
number of halves remaining in the fiscal year, including the half in which
application is made.
   (D)   Each individual business classification or individual business
activity conducted with and being included within said business classification
shall be assessed said license fee and each individual conducting such activity
shall obtain a license for each separate business classification and activity
in accordance with the listing below.
   (E)   All such annual license fees shall be paid at the Municipal Building
in the city, payable at the City Clerk’s office on or before June 30 for the
ensuing fiscal year, whereupon a license shall be issued by the City Clerk.
Said license shall be on such form or forms as prescribed by said Clerk.
   (F)   In the event that any such license provided from the state, or any
such agency thereof, is revoked, then in such event, any license provided by
reason of this section will likewise be revoked by said City Clerk without the
necessity of further proceedings hereunder.
   (G)   A business license is required by this chapter for every person
engaging in purposeful revenue generating activity in the city such as but not
limited to lawyers, doctors, architects, surveyors, real estate broker and
agents, accountants, engineers, nurses, LPNs, and the like. By way of
explanation, if there is a law office with three lawyers working in it, each
individual lawyer would each pay the business license tax.
   (H)   Any person engaging in business within the city shall pay an annual
general municipal business license tax of $10.
   (I)   A business license will be required for the following locations and
activities:
      (1)   A separate business license is required for each fixed business
location from which property or services are offered for sale or lease to the
public at a class, or to a limited portion of the public; or at which customer
accounts may be opened, closed or serviced.
      (2)   A separate business license is required for each coin-operated
machine. A separate license is required for each location from which making
coin-operated machines available to the public is itself a business activity.
      (3)   A business that sells tangible personal property or services from
or out of one or more vehicles needs a separate business license for each fixed
location in the city from or out of which business is conducted. A copy of its
business license shall be carried in each vehicle and publicly displayed while
business is conducted from or out of the vehicle.
      (4)   Nothing in this section and no payment or issuance of any
certificate of license under the provisions hereof, shall be deemed to legalize
any act which otherwise may be in violation of law, or to exempt any person
from any penalty prescribed for such violation.
      (5)   Every person to whom a certificate of license shall be issued under
the provisions of this chapter shall keep such certificate posted in a
conspicuous position in the place where the privileges of such license are
exercised, except as otherwise specifically provided for in this chapter. Such
certificate of license shall be produced for inspection whenever required by
the Director of Finance or his deputies or by the City Police.
      (6)   Every license issued under the provisions of this section shall
confer a personal privilege only to transact the business, activity, trade or
employment which may be the subject of the license and shall not be exercised
except by the person holding the same and shall not be assignable. Changes in
the name of the person or change of location, or address, or changes in
ownership of the business or changes in real parties of interest shall be
considered a cessation of the business and a new certificate shall be required.
Changes of partners or members of firms or officers of a corporation shall not
require a new certificate to be issued.

§ 110.99 PENALTY.
   Should any individual or business falling within a business classification
in accordance with the listing in §
110.01 and liable to pay an annual municipal license tax fail to secure such
license, such individual or legal representative of said business, shall be
liable for the assessment of $1 for each day said license fee is not paid in
accordance with the time schedule for payment set forth within this section.
Should any individual or legal representative of said business fail to obtain
any municipal license as provided herein, and as such violates any of the
foregoing provisions, such individual or legal representative shall be guilty
of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall be fined not less than $25
nor more than $500. The Municipal Court of the city shall have jurisdiction to
hear and determine all cases brought hereunder.
(Ord. 49, passed 2-26-1991)
CHAPTER 111: ALCOHOL
Section
   
111.01   Liquor license
 
   
111.99   Penalty
§ 111.01 LIQUOR LICENSE.
   (A)   As the state shall require a retail outlet to obtain a liquor license
from the state, the city shall also issue liquor licenses subsequent to the
retail outlet receiving a liquor license from the state. After the issuance of
a state liquor license, the applicant must then file an application with the
Clerk of the city.
   (B)   The annual retail license period shall be from July 1 to June 30 of
the following year. The annual retail license fee if an applicant holds a Class
A retail license under state law shall be the sum of $1,500 per outlet. The
annual retail license fee for the initial year of issuance shall be prorated
based on the number of days remaining between the date of issuance and the
following June 30.
   (C)   A retail license shall expire on June 30 of each year and may be
renewed only upon the submission of an application to the Clerk of the city.
   (D)   No person may sell liquor at any retail outlet if the retail license
applicable to such outlet has been suspended or revoked or has expired.
   (E)   All retail licenses issued or renewed under the provisions of this
section shall expire and be of no further force or effect as July 1, 2000.
Licenses issued thereafter will be issued in accordance with the applicable
law.
(Ord. 49, passed 2-26-1991) Penalty, see §
110.99
§ 111.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Should any individual or business that is liable to pay an annual
municipal license tax fail to secure such license, such individual or legal
representative of said business, shall be liable for the assessment of $1 for
each day said license fee is not paid in accordance with the time schedule for
payment set forth within this section. Should any individual or legal
representative of said business fail to obtain any municipal license as
provided herein, and as such violates any of the foregoing provisions, such
individual or legal representative shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and upon
conviction thereof shall be fined not less than $25 nor more than $500. The
Municipal Court of the city shall have jurisdiction to hear and determine all
cases brought hereunder.
   (B)   Violation of §
111.01(C) shall be punishable by a fine of $500 and/or imprisonment for up to
30 days.
(Ord. 49, passed 2-26-1991)
CHAPTER 112: SOLICITORS AND CANVASSERS
Section
   
112.01   Definitions
   
112.02   Registration required
   
112.03   Fee
   
112.04   Certificate
   
112.05   Exceptions
   
112.06   Period of solicitation
   
112.07   Revocation
   
112.08   Consent of occupant
 
   
112.99   Penalty
§ 112.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   SOLICITOR or CANVASSER. Includes any person or organization who takes orders
for future deliveries, or for intangible services, or solicits subscriptions or
contributions, in public places or from house to house and not from an
established place on private premises.
(Ord. 19, passed 2-27-1979)
§ 112.02 REGISTRATION REQUIRED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person or organization to engage in business as
canvasser or solicitor, calling at residences without the previous consent of
the occupant for the purpose of soliciting orders, sales, subscriptions,
contributions or business of any kind, or seeking for information or donations
without first having registered in the office of the City Clerk. The registrant
shall give his or her complete identification, his or her signature, the name
of his or her employer, the nature of the products or services in which he or
she is interested, the names of the manufacturers of such products, or of the
organization which he or she is representing, and the proposed method of
operation in the city.
(Ord. 19, passed 2-27-1979) Penalty, see §
112.99
§ 112.03 FEE.
   Each registrant shall pay to the City Clerk the annual business license fee
of $10 in accordance with
Chapter 110 for the hereinafter authorized period of solicitation or canvassing
which period shall begin on July 1 of each year commencing July 1, 2021, and
ending on June 30 of the following year, and if the initial license is granted
for less than a year, the fee shall be computed in proportion to the number of
halves remaining in the fiscal year, including the half in which application is
made.
(Ord. 19, passed 2-27-1979; Ord. passed 4-27-2021)
§ 112.04 CERTIFICATE.
   Each applicant who shows evidence of good character and who pays the fee
provided for herein shall be furnished a certificate indicating that he or she
has registered and showing the date such solicitation or canvassing is
authorized. Each and every person shall at all times while soliciting or
canvassing in the city carry upon his or her person the registration
certificate and the same shall be exhibited by such registrant whenever he or
she is required to do so by any police officer or by any persons solicited.
(Ord. 19, passed 2-27-1979)
§ 112.05 EXCEPTIONS.
   The provisions of this chapter shall not apply to all officers or employees
of the city, county, state or federal government, or any subdivision thereof,
when on official business. The provisions of this chapter shall also apply to
all societies, groups or organizations acting for charitable, religious or
benevolent purposes; provided, however, not registration fee will be charged to
such groups, by to obtain such registration receipt such representative shall
make an affidavit and produce such other evidence as to the fact entitling him
or her to such exemption as the City Clerk, in her or her discretion, may
require, which shall be on a form prescribed by the City Clerk.
(Ord. 19, passed 2-27-1979)
§ 112.06 PERIOD OF SOLICITATION.
   The authorized period of solicitation or canvassing will not exceed one day
in any one calendar year and will be confined between the hours of 9:00 a.m.
and 6:00 p.m. of that day; provided, however, exceptions to the authorized
period of solicitation or canvassing may be granted by the City Council for
cogent reasons set forth by such applicant and such approval being noted in the
minutes of a regular meeting of said Council.
(Ord. 19, passed 2-27-1979) Penalty, see §
112.99
§ 112.07 REVOCATION.
   Any such registration may be revoked by the Mayor or the Chief of Police
because of any violation by the registrant of this chapter or of any other
chapter of the city, or of any state of federal law, orwhenever the registrant
shall cease to possess the qualifications and character required in this
chapter of the original registration.
(Ord. 19, passed 2-27-1979)
§ 112.08 CONSENT OF OCCUPANT.
   The practice of going in and upon private residences in the city by
solicitors or canvassers, not having been requested or invited so to do by the
owner or owners, occupant or occupants of said private residences, for the
purpose of soliciting orders, sales, subscriptions, contributions or business
of any kind is declared to be a nuisance.
(Ord. 19, passed 2-27-1979) Penalty, see §
112.99
§ 112.99 PENALTY.
   Any person who is guilty of a violation of any provision of this chapter,
upon conviction thereof, shall be fined not less than $5 nor more than $100 for
each offense shall be deemed committed on each day during on or which a
violation occurs or continues.
(Ord. 19, passed 2-27-1979)
CHAPTER 113: NUDE DANCING
Section
   
113.01   Findings
   
113.02   Application of other provisions
   
113.03   Definitions
   
113.04   Employee conduct
   
113.05   Hours of operation
   
113.06   Location of nude dancing premises or adult entertainment premises
 
   
113.99   Penalty
§ 113.01 FINDINGS.
   Based on public input and other evidence and information before, the City
Council makes the following findings of fact.
   (A)   Certain conduct occurring on premises offering nude dancing is
detrimental to the public health, safety and general welfare of the citizens of
the city and, therefor, such conduct must be regulated as provided herein.
   (B)   Regulation of the nude dancing industry is necessary because in the
absence of such regulation the said nude dancing industry will: encourage
prostitution; increase sexual assaults; increase sexually transmitted diseases;
and attract other criminal activities.
(Ord. 62, passed 11-11-1997)
§ 113.02 APPLICATION OF OTHER PROVISIONS.
   The provisions of this chapter are not intended to supersede the provisions
of any other ordinance of the city, unless specifically set forth as such, or
the law of the state. The provisions of this chapter are in addition to any
other law or regulation.
(Ord. 62, passed 11-11-1997)
§ 113.03 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   EMPLOYEE. Any and all persons, including managers, entertainers and
independent contractors, who work in or at or render any services directly
related to, the operation of an adult entertainment premises.
   ENTERTAINER. Any person who on any occasion provides adult entertainment
within an adult entertainment premises as defined in this section, whether or
not a fee is charged or accepted for entertainment, or whether or not the
entertainer is paid.
   ENTERTAINMENT. Any exhibition or dance of any type, pantomime, modeling or
any other performance.
   MANAGER. Any person who manages, directs, administers or is in charge of,
the affairs and/or conduct of any portion of any activity involving adult
entertainment occurring at any adult entertainment premises.
   NUDE DANCING or DANCE NUDE. Any exhibition, performance or dance of any type
conducted in a premises where such exhibition, performance or dance involves a
person who:
      (1)   Is unclothed or in such attire, costume or clothing as to expose to
view any portion of the breast below the top of the areola or any portion of
the pubic region, anus, buttocks, vulva or genitals; or
      (2)   Touches, caresses or fondles the breast, buttocks, anus, genitals
or pubic region of a patron, or permits the touching, caressing or fondling of
his or her own breast, buttocks, anus, genitals or pubic region by a patron,
with the intent to sexually arouse or excite the patron.
   NUDE DANCING PREMISES or ADULT ENTERTAINMENT PREMISES. Any premises to which
the public, patrons or members are invited or admitted and wherein an
entertainer provides nude dancing or provides adult entertainment to a member
of the public, a patron or a member.
   OPERATOR. Any person operating, conducting or maintaining an adult
entertainment business or premises.
   PERSON. Any individual, partnership, corporation, trust, incorporated or
unincorporated association, marital community, joint venture or other entity or
group of persons however organized.
   PUBLIC PLACE. Any area generally visible to public view and includes
streets, sidewalks, bridges, alleys, plazas, parks, driveways, parking lots and
automobiles whether moving or not.
(Ord. 62, passed 11-11-1997)
§ 113.04 EMPLOYEE CONDUCT.
   The following standards of conduct upon the premises must be adhered to by
employees of any adult entertainment premises.
   (A)   No employee or entertainer shall be unclothed or in such less than
opaque and complete attire, costume or clothing so as to expose to view any
portion of the breast below the top of the areola or any portion of the pubic
region, anus, buttocks, vulva or genitals, except upon a stage where
entertainer shall wear at least pasties, G-string or similar item of clothing
to at least cover the areola, genitals and anal cleft.
   (B)   The stage shall be at least 24 inches above the immediate floor level
and removed at least ten feet from the nearest patron or person.
   (C)   No employee or entertainer mingling with any person or the patrons
shall be unclothed or in less than opaque and complete attire, costume or
clothing as described herein.
   (D)   No employee or entertainer shall knowingly permit any person upon the
premises to touch, caress or fondle the breasts, buttocks, anus or genitals of
any other person.
   (E)   No employee or entertainer shall touch, caress or fondle the breasts,
buttocks, anus or genitals of any other person.
   (F)   No employee or entertainer shall wear or use any device or covering
exposed to view which simulates the breast below the top of the areola, vulva
or genitals, anus, buttocks or any portion of the pubic region.
   (G)   No employee or entertainer shall use artificial devices or inanimate
objects to depict any of the prohibited activities described in this chapter.
   (H)   No employee or entertainer of any adult entertainment premises shall
be visible from any public place during the hours of his or her employment, or
apparent hours of his or her employment, on the premises.
   (I)   No entertainer shall solicit, demand or receive any payment or
gratuity from any patron for any act prohibited by this chapter.
(Ord. 62, passed 11-11-1997) Penalty, see §
113.99
§ 113.05 HOURS OF OPERATION.
   It is unlawful for any person to cause any nude dancing premises or adult
entertainment premises to remain open to the public, or to conduct or operate
business, whether for adult entertainment or otherwise, between the hours of 2:
00 a.m. and 6:00 p.m.
(Ord. 62, passed 11-11-1997) Penalty, see §
113.99
§ 113.06 LOCATION OF NUDE DANCING PREMISES OR ADULT ENTERTAINMENT PREMISES.
   (A)   No nude dancing premises or adult entertainment premises may be
located closer than 1,000 feet to the following places or specific areas:
      (1)   Any residential home, whether located in residential or business
district;
      (2)   Any private or public school;
      (3)   Any church or other type building where people gather to worship;
      (4)   Any public gathering area known as a community center, meeting area
or similar use, i.e. Community Building and Civic Center; and
      (5)   Any building or house which is used for the purpose of a form of
day care facility.
   (B)   This provision shall supersede any provision of the zoning regulations
of this city which is in conflict with the provisions contained herein.
(Ord. 62, passed 11-11-1997) Penalty, see §
113.99
§ 113.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to violate any provision of this
chapter; and whoever violates any provision of this chapter shall be fined not
more than $500. A person convicted of a second or subsequent offense under this
chapter, shall be fined not less than $300 and not more than $500 for each
violation.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any owner, proprietor or manager to operate
or own an adult entertainment establishment or nude dancing premises at such
time as any violation of this chapter or any portion of this chapter occurs.
Such violation is punishable by the same provisions set forth in division (A)
above.
(Ord. 62, passed 11-11-1997)
